<p><b>Trent John Alexander-Arnold</b> (born 7 October 1998) is an English professional <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">footballer</a> who plays as a <a href="/wiki/Right-back" class="mw-redirect" title="Right-back">right-back</a> for <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> club <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a> and the <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England national team</a>.
</p><p>Alexander-Arnold joined Liverpool's academy in 2004 and captained the club at across its youth levels. He made his senior debut in 2016, at age 18, and played in back-to-back <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> finals in <a href="/wiki/2018_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2018 UEFA Champions League Final">2018</a> and <a href="/wiki/2019_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2019 UEFA Champions League Final">2019</a>, winning the latter and being named in the Champions League Squad of the Season. These appearances made Alexander-Arnold the youngest player to start in consecutive finals in the competition. In the same year, he won the <a href="/wiki/2019_UEFA_Super_Cup" title="2019 UEFA Super Cup">UEFA Super Cup</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2019_FIFA_Club_World_Cup" title="2019 FIFA Club World Cup">FIFA Club World Cup</a>. In domestic football, Alexander-Arnold won the 2019–20 <a href="/wiki/PFA_Young_Player_of_the_Year" title="PFA Young Player of the Year">PFA Young Player of the Year</a> and the inaugural <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Young_Player_of_the_Season" title="Premier League Young Player of the Season">Premier League Young Player of the Season</a> awards, has twice been named in the <a href="/wiki/PFA_Team_of_the_Year" title="PFA Team of the Year">PFA Team of the Year</a>, and helped end Liverpool's <a href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%9320_Liverpool_F.C._season" title="2019–20 Liverpool F.C. season">30-year league title drought</a> by winning the <a href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%9320_Premier_League" title="2019–20 Premier League">2019–20 Premier League</a>.
</p><p>Alexander-Arnold has also represented England at various youth levels and made his senior debut in 2018. He has since featured at the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a>, where he became only the fourth teenager to start a match for England in the tournament, and in the <a href="/wiki/2018%E2%80%9319_UEFA_Nations_League" title="2018–19 UEFA Nations League">2018–19 UEFA Nations League</a> where his nation ended third.
</p>

<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#Honours"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Honours</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>
</ul>
</div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life_and_career">Early life and career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trent_Alexander-Arnold&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life and career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Alexander-Arnold was born in <a href="/wiki/West_Derby" title="West Derby">West Derby</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a>, where he attended St Matthew's Catholic Primary School, before later enrolling at <a href="/wiki/St_Mary%27s_College,_Crosby" title="St Mary&#39;s College, Crosby"> St Mary's</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Crosby,_Merseyside" title="Crosby, Merseyside">Crosby</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> When he was six years old, local football club <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a> hosted a half-term  camp to which a number of pupils from his school were invited, and his was one of the names drawn from a hat to attend. There, he was spotted by academy coach Ian Barrigan who subsequently approached his parents to offer him the chance to join the club's academy. He began training two-to-three times a week, and in a variety of different positions, before later going on to captain the club at U16 and U18 level under coach <a href="/wiki/Pepijn_Lijnders" title="Pepijn Lijnders">Pepijn Lijnders</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-JPA_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JPA-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> In the intervening period, at the age of 14, he left St. Mary's to enroll at <a href="/wiki/Rainhill_High_School" title="Rainhill High School">Rainhill High School</a>, an educational institution which shares an affiliation with the football club.<sup id="cite_ref-RB_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RB-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>It was also during his time in the academy that Alexander-Arnold converted from a <a href="/wiki/Winger_(sports)#Association_Football" title="Winger (sports)">winger</a> to a right-back as it was the position that offered him the clearest path to the first team and he excelled in his new role, being singled out by former Liverpool captain <a href="/wiki/Steven_Gerrard" title="Steven Gerrard">Steven Gerrard</a>, who tipped him to have a bright future at the club in his autobiography.<sup id="cite_ref-JPA_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JPA-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> As a result of his rapid progression, and in the buildup to the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_Liverpool_F.C._season" title="2015–16 Liverpool F.C. season">2015–16 season</a>, Alexander-Arnold was selected in the first team squad by <a href="/wiki/Manager_(association_football)" title="Manager (association football)">manager</a> <a href="/wiki/Brendan_Rodgers" title="Brendan Rodgers">Brendan Rodgers</a> for the team's final pre-season <a href="/wiki/Exhibition_game#Association_football" title="Exhibition game">friendly</a> against <a href="/wiki/Swindon_Town_F.C." title="Swindon Town F.C.">Swindon Town</a> where he marked his unofficial debut for the club in a 2–1 win.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_career">Club career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trent_Alexander-Arnold&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Club career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Liverpool">Liverpool</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trent_Alexander-Arnold&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Liverpool">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span id="2016.E2.80.9317_season:_Development_and_breakthrough"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2016–17_season:_Development_and_breakthrough">2016–17 season: Development and breakthrough</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trent_Alexander-Arnold&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 2016–17 season: Development and breakthrough">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Having previously taken part in Liverpool's pre-season tour of the United States, Alexander-Arnold made his professional debut on 25 October 2016, starting in a 2–1 victory over <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a> in the fourth round of the <a href="/wiki/EFL_Cup" title="EFL Cup">EFL Cup</a>. He was <a href="/wiki/Penalty_card#Yellow_card" title="Penalty card">booked</a> in the first half for a foul on <a href="/wiki/Ben_Davies_(footballer,_born_1993)" title="Ben Davies (footballer, born 1993)">Ben Davies</a>, which he later revealed could have ended in him being sent off, before being <a href="/wiki/Substitute_(association_football)" title="Substitute (association football)">substituted</a> for first-choice right-back <a href="/wiki/Nathaniel_Clyne" title="Nathaniel Clyne">Nathaniel Clyne</a> in the 68th minute.<sup id="cite_ref-JPA_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JPA-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Despite the indiscretion, his performance was lauded by Gerrard who once again backed him "to become a top professional", and also earned a spot in the EFL Cup Team of the Round alongside teammate <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Sturridge" title="Daniel Sturridge">Daniel Sturridge</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Uncle_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Uncle-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Trent_Alexander_Arnold_2016.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Trent_Alexander_Arnold_2016.jpg/170px-Trent_Alexander_Arnold_2016.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="257" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Trent_Alexander_Arnold_2016.jpg/255px-Trent_Alexander_Arnold_2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Trent_Alexander_Arnold_2016.jpg/340px-Trent_Alexander_Arnold_2016.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1495" data-file-height="2264" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Trent_Alexander_Arnold_2016.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Alexander-Arnold, pictured here in match against <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C._Under-23s_and_Academy" title="Arsenal F.C. Under-23s and Academy">Arsenal U18</a> in 2016, captained the <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C._Reserves_and_Academy" title="Liverpool F.C. Reserves and Academy">Liverpool U18</a> side during his time in the academy.</div></div></div>
<p>Alexander-Arnold's breakthrough into the first team was rewarded with a new long-term contract in November and he started in Liverpool's next EFL Cup match later that month against <a href="/wiki/Leeds_United_F.C." title="Leeds United F.C.">Leeds United</a>. He was named <a href="/wiki/Man_of_the_Match" class="mw-redirect" title="Man of the Match">Man of the Match</a> for his performance after registering his first <a href="/wiki/Assist_(football)" class="mw-redirect" title="Assist (football)">assist</a> for the club by setting up <a href="/wiki/Forward_(association_football)" title="Forward (association football)">striker</a> <a href="/wiki/Divock_Origi" title="Divock Origi">Divock Origi</a> for the opening goal of a 2–0 win for Liverpool.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> He then made his Premier League debut on 14 December, coming on as a late substitute in a 3–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_F.C." title="Middlesbrough F.C.">Middlesbrough</a>, and made his first league start in a 1–1 draw with <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> on 15 January 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> In May, having made 12 appearances across all competitions, he was named Liverpool's Young Player of the Season and was also nominated for the <a href="/wiki/Professional_Development_League" title="Professional Development League">Premier League 2</a> Player of the Season award.<sup id="cite_ref-AK_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AK-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-YPOTY_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YPOTY-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2017.E2.80.9318_season:_First_Champions_League_Final"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2017–18_season:_First_Champions_League_Final">2017–18 season: First Champions League Final</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trent_Alexander-Arnold&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2017–18 season: First Champions League Final">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In the buildup to the <a href="/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_Liverpool_F.C._season" title="2017–18 Liverpool F.C. season">2017–18 season</a>, regular right-back Clyne suffered a serious back injury which afforded Alexander-Arnold the opportunity to rotate with <a href="/wiki/Joe_Gomez_(footballer)" title="Joe Gomez (footballer)">Joe Gomez</a> during the early stages of the campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> On 15 August 2017, he scored his first goal for the club when he struck home from a <a href="/wiki/Direct_free_kick" class="mw-redirect" title="Direct free kick">free kick</a> in a 2–1 first leg <a href="/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2017–18 UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a> play-off round win over <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga" title="Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a> team <a href="/wiki/TSG_1899_Hoffenheim" title="TSG 1899 Hoffenheim">Hoffenheim</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> In doing so, he became the third youngest player to score on his European debut for Liverpool, after <a href="/wiki/Michael_Owen" title="Michael Owen">Michael Owen</a> and <a href="/wiki/David_Fairclough" title="David Fairclough">David Fairclough</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> During the group stages of the competition, Alexander-Arnold scored again in a 7–0 <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a> win over <a href="/wiki/NK_Maribor" title="NK Maribor">Maribor</a> on 17 October, a result which was the joint-largest ever away win in the competition, and largest away win by an English club.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> He then scored his first Premier League goal for Liverpool on <a href="/wiki/Boxing_Day" title="Boxing Day">Boxing Day</a>, netting in a 5–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Swansea_City_F.C." class="mw-redirect" title="Swansea City F.C.">Swansea City</a> at <a href="/wiki/Anfield" title="Anfield">Anfield</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:237px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Spartak_Moscow-_Liverpool.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Spartak_Moscow-_Liverpool.jpg/235px-Spartak_Moscow-_Liverpool.jpg" decoding="async" width="235" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Spartak_Moscow-_Liverpool.jpg/353px-Spartak_Moscow-_Liverpool.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Spartak_Moscow-_Liverpool.jpg/470px-Spartak_Moscow-_Liverpool.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1275" data-file-height="850" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Spartak_Moscow-_Liverpool.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Alexander-Arnold (bottom, left-centre) lining-up for <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a> in a <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a> match against <a href="/wiki/FC_Spartak_Moscow" title="FC Spartak Moscow">Spartak Moscow</a> in 2017.</div></div></div>
<p>In March the following year, Alexander-Arnold endured his most difficult spell with the club to date, after struggling against <a href="/wiki/Crystal_Palace_F.C." title="Crystal Palace F.C.">Crystal Palace</a> winger <a href="/wiki/Wilfried_Zaha" title="Wilfried Zaha">Wilfried Zaha</a> and Manchester United's <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Rashford" title="Marcus Rashford">Marcus Rashford</a> in successive weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-JPA_7-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JPA-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Nonetheless, he retained his position in Liverpool's starting line-up to become the youngest English player to start in a Champions League quarter-final match and performed strongly in a 3–0 win over English rivals <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester City">Manchester City</a> in April. His performance saw him named Man of the Match and earned him praise from the media for his ability to nullify City winger <a href="/wiki/Leroy_San%C3%A9" title="Leroy Sané">Leroy Sané</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> He impressed again in the reverse fixture as Liverpool eliminated City 5–1 on <a href="/wiki/Two-legged_tie" title="Two-legged tie">aggregate</a> to advance to the semi-finals of the competition for the first time in 10 years.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> On 10 May, his domestic and European form was rewarded when he won the Liverpool Young Player of the Season award for the second season running.<sup id="cite_ref-YPOTY2_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YPOTY2-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> Later that month, he became the youngest Liverpool player to start in a <a href="/wiki/2018_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2018 UEFA Champions League Final">Champions League final</a> when he was named in the starting line-up against two-time reigning champions, <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF" title="Real Madrid CF">Real Madrid</a>. Tasked with marking <a href="/wiki/Cristiano_Ronaldo" title="Cristiano Ronaldo">Cristiano Ronaldo</a>, he performed admirably though Liverpool ultimately succumbed to a 3–1 defeat.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Following the conclusion of the season, in which he scored three goals in 33 appearances across all competitions, he was nominated for the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Boy_(award)" title="Golden Boy (award)">Golden Boy</a> award where he was later voted runner-up to <a href="/wiki/AFC_Ajax" title="AFC Ajax">Ajax</a> defender, <a href="/wiki/Matthijs_de_Ligt" title="Matthijs de Ligt">Matthijs de Ligt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2018.E2.80.9319_season:_Regular_starter_and_Champions_League_title"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2018–19_season:_Regular_starter_and_Champions_League_title">2018–19 season: Regular starter and Champions League title</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trent_Alexander-Arnold&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2018–19 season: Regular starter and Champions League title">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>During the early stages of the <a href="/wiki/2018%E2%80%9319_Premier_League" title="2018–19 Premier League">following season</a>, he made his 50th appearance for Liverpool when he started in a 2–1 victory over Tottenham; the same opposition against whom he had made his debut almost two years prior.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> In October, he was one of 10 players nominated for the inaugural <a href="/wiki/Kopa_Trophy" title="Kopa Trophy">Kopa Trophy</a>, an award presented by <i><a href="/wiki/France_Football" title="France Football">France Football</a></i> to the best young player under the age of 21, and ultimately ended sixth in the voting polls, having received votes from Owen, <a href="/wiki/Denis_Law" title="Denis Law">Denis Law</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pavel_Nedv%C4%9Bd" title="Pavel Nedvd">Pavel Nedvd</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> He continued to enhance his burgeoning reputation in the months thereafter and was consistently listed in reports by the <a href="/wiki/International_Centre_for_Sports_Studies" title="International Centre for Sports Studies">CIES</a> as the world's most valuable full-back from a transfer value perspective.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Alexander-Arnold elevated his game further following the turn of the year and, on 27 February 2019, became the youngest player, aged 20 years and 143 days, to record three assists in a single Premier League match when he set up <a href="/wiki/Sadio_Man%C3%A9" title="Sadio Mané">Sadio Mané</a> twice and <a href="/wiki/Virgil_van_Dijk" title="Virgil van Dijk">Virgil van Dijk</a> once in a 5–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Watford_F.C." title="Watford F.C.">Watford</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-eply_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eply-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Less than two months later,  he became the fifth-youngest player to reach 50 Premier League appearances for the club, behind Owen, <a href="/wiki/Raheem_Sterling" title="Raheem Sterling">Raheem Sterling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robbie_Fowler" title="Robbie Fowler">Robbie Fowler</a> and Gerrard, when he started in a 3–1 win over <a href="/wiki/Southampton_F.C." title="Southampton F.C.">Southampton</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> His domestic form was rewarded later in April when he was nominated for the <a href="/wiki/PFA_Young_Player_of_the_Year" title="PFA Young Player of the Year">PFA Young Player of the Year</a> award, although the award was won by Manchester City's Sterling, and he was later named in the <a href="/wiki/PFA_Team_of_the_Year" title="PFA Team of the Year">PFA Team of the Year</a> alongside Liverpool teammates  van Dijk, Mané and <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Robertson" title="Andrew Robertson">Andrew Robertson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LFC_Parade_2019_01_Trent_Alexander-Arnold.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/LFC_Parade_2019_01_Trent_Alexander-Arnold.jpg/170px-LFC_Parade_2019_01_Trent_Alexander-Arnold.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="248" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/LFC_Parade_2019_01_Trent_Alexander-Arnold.jpg/255px-LFC_Parade_2019_01_Trent_Alexander-Arnold.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/LFC_Parade_2019_01_Trent_Alexander-Arnold.jpg/340px-LFC_Parade_2019_01_Trent_Alexander-Arnold.jpg 2x" data-file-width="577" data-file-height="841" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:LFC_Parade_2019_01_Trent_Alexander-Arnold.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Alexander-Arnold during Liverpool's Champions League victory parade, 2019.</div></div></div>
<p>His creative prowess came to the fore once again in May when, during a 3–2 win over <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C." title="Newcastle United F.C.">Newcastle United</a>, Alexander-Arnold equalled the Premier League record for the most assists by a defender in a season, with his two assists in the match raising his tally to 11. It also saw him and Robertson, who had 11 assists of his own, become the first set of defenders from the same team to record double figures for assists in the same season.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Three days later, with Liverpool trailing <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">Barcelona</a> 3–0 on aggregate after a first-leg defeat, he recorded two more assists, including an "instinctive corner" for Origi's winning goal, to help the club to a 4–3 aggregate victory and progress to a second consecutive Champions League final.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> On the final day of the domestic season, Alexander-Arnold assisted Mané in a 2–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Wolverhampton_Wanderers_F.C." title="Wolverhampton Wanderers F.C.">Wolverhampton Wanderers</a> to break the Premier League record for the most assists by a defender in a domestic campaign, with 12, surpassing previous holders <a href="/wiki/Andy_Hinchcliffe" title="Andy Hinchcliffe">Andy Hinchcliffe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leighton_Baines" title="Leighton Baines">Leighton Baines</a> and Robertson.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> He then started in the <a href="/wiki/2019_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2019 UEFA Champions League Final">Champions League Final</a>, a 2–0 win over Tottenham, and became the youngest player to start in two successive finals in the competition, breaking the record set by <a href="/wiki/A.C._Milan" title="A.C. Milan">A.C. Milan</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Christian_Panucci" title="Christian Panucci">Christian Panucci</a> in 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-ucly_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ucly-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> He was later named in the competition's Team of the Season and nominated for the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Club_Football_Awards#Best_Defender" title="UEFA Club Football Awards">Defender of the Season</a> award.<sup id="cite_ref-cltots_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cltots-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2019.E2.80.9320_season:_Ballon_d.27Or_nomination_and_Premier_League_title"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2019–20_season:_Ballon_d'Or_nomination_and_Premier_League_title">2019–20 season: Ballon d'Or nomination and Premier League title</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trent_Alexander-Arnold&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2019–20 season: Ballon d&#039;Or nomination and Premier League title">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Liverpool_vs._Chelsea,_UEFA_Super_Cup_2019-08-14_53.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Liverpool_vs._Chelsea%2C_UEFA_Super_Cup_2019-08-14_53.jpg/220px-Liverpool_vs._Chelsea%2C_UEFA_Super_Cup_2019-08-14_53.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Liverpool_vs._Chelsea%2C_UEFA_Super_Cup_2019-08-14_53.jpg/330px-Liverpool_vs._Chelsea%2C_UEFA_Super_Cup_2019-08-14_53.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Liverpool_vs._Chelsea%2C_UEFA_Super_Cup_2019-08-14_53.jpg/440px-Liverpool_vs._Chelsea%2C_UEFA_Super_Cup_2019-08-14_53.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1050" data-file-height="700" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Liverpool_vs._Chelsea,_UEFA_Super_Cup_2019-08-14_53.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Alexander-Arnold (far right) celebrates Liverpool's <a href="/wiki/2019_UEFA_Super_Cup" title="2019 UEFA Super Cup">2019 UEFA Super Cup</a> victory over <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Alexander-Arnold began the <a href="/wiki/2019-20_Liverpool_F.C._season" class="mw-redirect" title="2019-20 Liverpool F.C. season">2019–20</a> campaign with his position as Liverpool's right-back cemented, and provided the assist for Origi's goal in the club's 4–1 opening game win over <a href="/wiki/Norwich_F.C." class="mw-redirect" title="Norwich F.C.">Norwich</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-IrTimes1_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IrTimes1-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> In doing so, he became only the eighth player in the Premier League era to register an assist in five consecutive games, and the first to do so for Liverpool.<sup id="cite_ref-Squawka_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Squawka-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> He appeared in subsequent wins over <a href="/wiki/Southampton_F.C." title="Southampton F.C.">Southampton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a>, as well as in Liverpool's triumph over <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2019_UEFA_Super_Cup" title="2019 UEFA Super Cup">UEFA Super Cup</a> where he scored a penalty in the shoot-out.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian1_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian1-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> He then scored his first goal of the season during Liverpool's 2–1 league win over the Blues from a set-piece routine that was later nominated for the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Goal_of_the_Month" title="Premier League Goal of the Month">Premier League Goal of the Month</a> award.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> The following month, he was nominated for the <a href="/wiki/2019_Ballon_d%27Or" title="2019 Ballon d&#39;Or">2019 Ballon d'Or</a> award, alongside six of his Liverpool teammates.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 2 November, at the age of 21 years and 26 days, he became the fourth-youngest player to reach 100 appearances for Liverpool, behind Owen, Sterling and Fowler, and marked the occasion by assisting Mané for the winning goal in a 2–1 victory over <a href="/wiki/Aston_Villa_F.C." title="Aston Villa F.C.">Aston Villa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Exactly one month later, he was voted as the 19th-best player in the world at the Ballon d'Or ceremony, and the highest-ranked full-back.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> He then made his <a href="/wiki/FIFA_Club_World_Cup" title="FIFA Club World Cup">FIFA Club World Cup</a> debut during Liverpool's 2–1 semi-final win over reigning <a href="/wiki/CONCACAF_Champions_League" title="CONCACAF Champions League">CONCACAF</a> champions <a href="/wiki/C.F._Monterrey" title="C.F. Monterrey">Monterrey</a>, and provided the match-winning assist for <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Firmino" title="Roberto Firmino">Roberto Firmino</a> in stoppage time after coming on as a substitute for <a href="/wiki/James_Milner" title="James Milner">James Milner</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Three days later, he started and played the full 120 minutes as Liverpool were crowned champions for the first time in the club's history following a 1–0 win after <a href="/wiki/Overtime_(sports)#Association_football" title="Overtime (sports)">extra-time</a> over <a href="/wiki/Copa_Libertadores" title="Copa Libertadores">Copa Libertadores</a> champions <a href="/wiki/Clube_de_Regatas_do_Flamengo" title="Clube de Regatas do Flamengo">Flamengo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Upon returning from Qatar, Liverpool recorded a 4–0 league win over second-placed <a href="/wiki/Leicester_City_F.C." title="Leicester City F.C.">Leicester City</a> during a match in which Alexander-Arnold played a hand in all four goals by scoring one, assisting two, and winning a penalty which was converted by Milner.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> He was later rewarded for his form with the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Player_of_the_Month" title="Premier League Player of the Month">Premier League Player of the Month</a> award, becoming the first full-back to claim the honour since <a href="/wiki/Micah_Richards" title="Micah Richards">Micah Richards</a> in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> Further recognition followed at the turn of the year, when he was named in the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Team_of_the_Year#Team_of_the_Year_2019" title="UEFA Team of the Year">2019 UEFA Team of the Year</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UTOTY_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UTOTY-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> Alexander-Arnold then played a starring role in Liverpool's 2–1 win over Wolves as the club extended their unbeaten run in the league to 40 matches. During the encounter, he assisted captain <a href="/wiki/Jordan_Henderson" title="Jordan Henderson">Jordan Henderson</a> for the opening goal and in the process became the first defender in the competition's history to reach double figures for assists in multiple campaigns.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Towards the end of February, following a 3–2 win over <a href="/wiki/West_Ham_United_F.C." title="West Ham United F.C.">West Ham United</a>, he matched his league assist record from the campaign before and took his overall tally in the Premier League to 25, becoming the third-youngest player in the competition's history to reach a quarter-century of assists behind <a href="/wiki/Cesc_F%C3%A0bregas" title="Cesc Fàbregas">Cesc Fàbregas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Rooney" title="Wayne Rooney">Wayne Rooney</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> The season was temporarily suspended between March and June due to the outbreak of the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>, following which Alexander-Arnold helped Liverpool win their first league title in 30 years, and their first in the Premier League era.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> With the title secured, he then broke his own assist record on the penultimate day of the campaign when he set Firmino up to score in a 5–3 win over Chelsea.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> For his contributions during the season, he was awarded the inaugural <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Young_Player_of_the_Season" title="Premier League Young Player of the Season">Premier League Young Player of the Season</a> award, won the PFA Young Player of the Year accolade and was named in the PFA Team of the Year.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2020.E2.80.9321_season:_Further_career_milestones"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2020–21_season:_Further_career_milestones">2020–21 season: Further career milestones</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trent_Alexander-Arnold&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2020–21 season: Further career milestones">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On 9 December, he became the youngest-ever player to captain Liverpool in European competition, and third-youngest in any competition for the club, when he donned the armband during the Reds' 1–1 <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> draw against <a href="/wiki/FC_Midtjylland" title="FC Midtjylland">FC Midtjylland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Later that month, he was named in the 2020 <a href="/wiki/FIFPro#FIFA_FIFPro_Men&#39;s_World11" title="FIFPro">FIFA FIFPro Men's World XI</a> alongside Liverpool teammates <a href="/wiki/Alisson_Becker" class="mw-redirect" title="Alisson Becker">Alisson Becker</a>, Van Dijk and <a href="/wiki/Thiago_Alc%C3%A2ntara" title="Thiago Alcântara">Thiago Alcântara</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FIFPro_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FIFPro-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> On 28 January 2021, he scored his first goal of the season in a 3–1 away league win over Tottenham.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_career">International career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trent_Alexander-Arnold&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: International career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Youth">Youth</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trent_Alexander-Arnold&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Youth">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Trent_Alexander-Arnold.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Trent_Alexander-Arnold.jpg/170px-Trent_Alexander-Arnold.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="271" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Trent_Alexander-Arnold.jpg/255px-Trent_Alexander-Arnold.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Trent_Alexander-Arnold.jpg/340px-Trent_Alexander-Arnold.jpg 2x" data-file-width="524" data-file-height="836" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Trent_Alexander-Arnold.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Alexander-Arnold represented <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a> in Russia.</div></div></div>
<p>Alexander-Arnold has represented England at various youth levels and featured at the <a href="/wiki/2015_FIFA_U-17_World_Cup" title="2015 FIFA U-17 World Cup">2015 FIFA U-17 World Cup</a> in Chile.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> He also scored three goals for the <a href="/wiki/England_national_under-19_football_team" title="England national under-19 football team">England U19</a> team, including a brace against <a href="/wiki/Croatia_national_under-19_football_team" title="Croatia national under-19 football team">Croatia</a> and another against <a href="/wiki/Spain_national_under-19_football_team" title="Spain national under-19 football team">Spain</a> which secured England's qualification for the <a href="/wiki/2017_UEFA_European_Under-19_Championship" title="2017 UEFA European Under-19 Championship">2017 UEFA European Under-19 Championship</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> He did not feature at the tournament itself as Liverpool reached an agreement with England to rest him ahead of the following season's league campaign, but the Three Lions went on to defeat <a href="/wiki/Portugal_national_under-19_football_team" title="Portugal national under-19 football team">Portugal</a> in the final to claim their first ever title in the competition.<sup id="cite_ref-AK_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AK-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> The month following the tournament, he was called up to the <a href="/wiki/England_national_under-21_football_team" title="England national under-21 football team">England U21</a> team for the first time for their <a href="/wiki/2019_UEFA_European_Under-21_Championship_qualification" title="2019 UEFA European Under-21 Championship qualification">UEFA European Under-21 Championship qualifiers</a> against <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_under-21_football_team" title="Netherlands national under-21 football team">Netherlands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Latvia_national_under-21_football_team" title="Latvia national under-21 football team">Latvia</a>, and made his debut in a 3–0 win over the latter. Two more appearances followed with the U21 side before he was promoted and solidified his status within the senior <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a> camp.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Senior">Senior</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trent_Alexander-Arnold&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Senior">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In March 2018, while part of the U21 team, Alexander-Arnold was invited to train with the <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">senior national team</a> for the first time ahead of their friendly matches against <a href="/wiki/Italy_national_football_team" title="Italy national football team">Italy</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_football_team" title="Netherlands national football team">Netherlands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> He received his first call-up in May 2018 when he was named in <a href="/wiki/Gareth_Southgate" title="Gareth Southgate">Gareth Southgate</a>'s squad for the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> His debut followed on 7 June 2018 when he started in a 2–0 pre-tournament friendly win over <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica_national_football_team" title="Costa Rica national football team">Costa Rica</a> at <a href="/wiki/Elland_Road" title="Elland Road">Elland Road</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> Prior to the match, he was handed his match jersey by <a href="/wiki/Prince_William,_Duke_of_Cambridge" title="Prince William, Duke of Cambridge">Prince William, Duke of Cambridge</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> Alexander-Arnold then made his debut in the competition on 28 June, starting in a 1–0 group-stage defeat to <a href="/wiki/Belgium_national_football_team" title="Belgium national football team">Belgium</a>, after both sides had already confirmed their progression to the knockout stages. In doing so, he became only the fourth teenager to start a match for England at a World Cup.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> It remained, however, his only appearance as <a href="/wiki/Kieran_Trippier" title="Kieran Trippier">Kieran Trippier</a> was preferred at right-back and featured throughout as England were defeated by <a href="/wiki/Croatia_national_football_team" title="Croatia national football team">Croatia</a> in the semi-finals, and then again by Belgium in the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_knockout_stage#Third_place_play-off" title="2018 FIFA World Cup knockout stage">third place play-off</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 15 November 2018, during a friendly international, held in honour of Wayne Rooney, Alexander-Arnold scored his first senior international goal as England recorded a 3–0 win over the <a href="/wiki/United_States_men%27s_national_soccer_team" title="United States men&#39;s national soccer team">United States</a> at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley Stadium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> In doing so, and at the age of 20 years and 39 days, he became the youngest Liverpool player since Michael Owen in 1999 to score for the national team.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> In June 2019, he was part of the England squad which ended third at the inaugural <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Nations_League" title="UEFA Nations League">UEFA Nations League</a> and played the full match in a <a href="/wiki/Penalty_shoot-out_(association_football)" title="Penalty shoot-out (association football)">penalty shoot-out</a> win over <a href="/wiki/Switzerland_national_football_team" title="Switzerland national football team">Switzerland</a> in the third-place play-off.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Style_of_play">Style of play</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trent_Alexander-Arnold&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Style of play">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Alexander-Arnold is widely regarded as one of the best attacking full-backs in world football as a result of his proficiency at occupying attacking spaces on the pitch and creating goalscoring opportunities for his teammates.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> During the early years of his career, he emerged as one of the Premier League's most creative players due to his role in assisting goals from early <a href="/wiki/Cross_(association_football)" title="Cross (association football)">crosses</a> and set-piece deliveries.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> He possesses an impressive passing range, which is attributed to his development as a <a href="/wiki/Midfielder" title="Midfielder">midfielder</a> during his time in Liverpool's youth academy, and has been one of Liverpool's designated set-piece specialists for deadball situations since the <a href="/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_Liverpool_F.C._season" title="2017–18 Liverpool F.C. season">2017–18 campaign</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-sop1_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sop1-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sop2_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sop2-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> His set-piece routine, which involves three parallel steps backwards and one to the right, has been likened to that of former <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a> <a href="/wiki/Fly-half" class="mw-redirect" title="Fly-half">fly-half</a> <a href="/wiki/Jonny_Wilkinson" title="Jonny Wilkinson">Jonny Wilkinson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-sop3_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sop3-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Under Liverpool manager <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BCrgen_Klopp" title="Jürgen Klopp">Jürgen Klopp</a>, whose tactical set-up placed creative responsibility on the shoulders of the club's full-backs, Alexander-Arnold was predominantly deployed down the right flank where his overlapping runs, switching of play, accuracy of crossing and work-rate in tracking back saw him become an important figure in the side's transitional, counter-attacking style of play.<sup id="cite_ref-sop3_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sop3-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Alexander-Arnold's craft and intelligence were singled out for particular praise by <a href="/wiki/Gary_Lineker" title="Gary Lineker">Gary Lineker</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cesc_F%C3%A0bregas" title="Cesc Fàbregas">Cesc Fàbregas</a> after his assist for the winning goal in the 2018–19 Champions League semi-final, in which he delivered a corner while the opposition players had their backs turned.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trent_Alexander-Arnold&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Melwood5.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Melwood5.jpg/170px-Melwood5.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Melwood5.jpg/255px-Melwood5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Melwood5.jpg/340px-Melwood5.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="1280" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Melwood5.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Alexander-Arnold was born in <a href="/wiki/West_Derby" title="West Derby">West Derby</a>; a short distance from <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool's</a> training ground, <a href="/wiki/Melwood" title="Melwood">Melwood</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Alexander-Arnold is the nephew of former <a href="/wiki/Reading_F.C." title="Reading F.C.">Reading</a> and <a href="/wiki/Millwall_F.C." title="Millwall F.C.">Millwall</a> footballer, and former Manchester United club secretary, <a href="/wiki/John_Alexander_(footballer,_born_1955)" title="John Alexander (footballer, born 1955)">John Alexander</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Uncle_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Uncle-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> His maternal grandmother, Doreen Carling, was once also in a relationship with former United manager, <a href="/wiki/Sir_Alex_Ferguson" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Alex Ferguson">Sir Alex Ferguson</a>, before moving to New York City where she later married. Alexander-Arnold was thus eligible to play for the <a href="/wiki/United_States_men%27s_national_soccer_team" title="United States men&#39;s national soccer team">United States</a> prior to making his England debut.<sup id="cite_ref-TG_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TG-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> He has two brothers; Tyler, who is four years his senior and acts as his <a href="/wiki/Sports_agent" title="Sports agent">agent</a>, and Marcel, who is three years younger.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Outside of football, Alexander-Arnold volunteers as an ambassador for the Liverpool-based charity <i>An Hour for Others</i>, which seeks to provide underprivileged members of the community with anything from food hampers and toys to cooking and science lessons. He has supported the charity since being introduced to it by his mother in his mid-teens. During his time with Liverpool's academy, he and teammate Kris Owens pledged to support the initiative if either of them made it as professional footballers.<sup id="cite_ref-TG_107-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TG-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> His philanthropy also expands beyond the charity and in March 2019, after signing a new boot sponsorship with <a href="/wiki/Under_Armour" title="Under Armour">Under Armour</a> (the second most lucrative boot deal in England behind <a href="/wiki/Harry_Kane" title="Harry Kane">Harry Kane</a>'s) he initiated plans to purchase plots in Liverpool and use the funds to construct new pitches for the community.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He is also an avid <a href="/wiki/Chess" title="Chess">chess</a> player, having been introduced to the sport by his father as a youngster, and in 2018 he played an invitational match against world champion <a href="/wiki/Magnus_Carlsen" title="Magnus Carlsen">Magnus Carlsen</a>. The match, which was played as part of a campaign to promote the sport, ended in defeat for Alexander-Arnold after seventeen moves; eight more than technology entrepreneur <a href="/wiki/Bill_Gates" title="Bill Gates">Bill Gates</a> managed when he faced Carlsen in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> Alexander-Arnold later explained how chess was more than just a pastime and had helped him in his football career by teaching him to think "two or three moves ahead of the opposition".<sup id="cite_ref-RB_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RB-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2020, he and fellow Liverpool full-back <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Robertson" title="Andrew Robertson">Andrew Robertson</a> starred in their own digital series on <a href="/wiki/IGTV" title="IGTV">IGTV</a> called 'Wingmen'.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Honours">Honours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trent_Alexander-Arnold&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Honours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LFC_Parade_2019_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/LFC_Parade_2019_01.jpg/220px-LFC_Parade_2019_01.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/LFC_Parade_2019_01.jpg/330px-LFC_Parade_2019_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/LFC_Parade_2019_01.jpg/440px-LFC_Parade_2019_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6016" data-file-height="4016" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:LFC_Parade_2019_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Alexander-Arnold (far right) was part of the Liverpool squad which won the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> trophy in 2019.</div></div></div>
